Getting Started
Autopilot Software 

The computer itself is a mini motherboard ([ext[Commell LS-37B|http://www.commell.com.tw/product/SBC/LS-37B.HTM]]) running a stock version of the Ubuntu Linux operating system. 

The computer interacts with the helicopter via the [[Servo Switch]] and the [[Engine Control Unit]] (both via serial) as well as with any other hardware devices through serial/USB ports or network ports.

The following is an overview of the hardware devices and I/O for the autopilot computer:

;Motherboard ([ext[Commell LS-37B|http://www.commell.com.tw/product/SBC/LS-37B.HTM]])

* Serial port(s)
** [[Servo Switch]]
* LAN port(s)
** [[Microhard Radio]]
* ~WiFi
** Card available, but not being used currently
* USB (2 ports, +2 optional breakout)
** [[GX3 Inertial Measurement Unit]] (IMU) [Serial -> USB]
** [[Novatel GPS]] [Serial -> USB]
** [[Engine Control Unit]] (ECU) Communication [Serial -> USB]
** [[MDL Altimeter]] [Serial -> USB]
*Power
** Outboard Battery (12V) [attached to helicopter]
*** -> Motherboard
*** -> [[Servo Switch]]
*** -> [[Microhard Radio]]
*** -> [2x parallel: Pololu 3.3V 500mA ~Step-Down circuit boards]
**** -> Novatel GPS
* Power/Reset Switch
** Connects to 5th set of jumpers from the outside edge of the motherboard

;3D Printed Box Enclosure

* Provides housing for: 
** Mini motherboard
** [[Novatel GPS]]
** [[Servo Switch]]
** [[Microhard Radio]]
* Additional enclosure details:
** Hole for servo switch breakout
** Hole for onboard USB ports
** Hole for momentary reset switch
** Holes for radio antennae
** Hole for Novatel GPS antenna
** Top holes for ventilation (CPU fan)
** Other holes for cabling
* 3D Printers Available:
** Stratasys 3D printer: Located in DU Metallurgy building
** Makerbot: ??
* Sketchup file for box located in autopilot repository:
**autopilot/hardware/box3.skp
** Enclosure requires some additional routing/dremel-ing to fit everything

;Ubuntu Linux System

*Radio communication requires that the autopilot computer be setup with a static IP address
* Verified working with Ubuntu 13.10, Mint 17
The autopilot software is written primarily in C++. The main components of the software are as follows:

;Main App
:The software initializes and runs its main loop in the [[MainApp class]]. In this class all drivers are instantiated and then the autopilot goes into a control loop that communicates with the servo switch in the way designated by the current control mode (DIRECT_MANUAL, SCALED_MANUAL, AUTOMATIC_CONTROL).

;Device Drivers
:These should implement the [[Driver class]], which has methods to initialize the driver, run the driver loop in its own thread, build/send/recieve [[MAVLink Messages]], and terminate the driver. The following are currently implemented drivers:

* [[GX3 Inertial Measurement Device]]
* [[Novatel GPS]]
* [[MDL Altimeter]]
* Linux (CPU usage/RAM usage)
* [[Servo Switch]]
* [[QGCLink]] (communication with [[QGroundControl]])
* [[Waypoint Manager]]
* Common Messages (send/receive variety of common MAVLink messages)

;Control Models
:This is a set of classes and utilities that deal with calculating servo speeds for maintaining helicopter stability and movement.
* Probably need more information here

;Configuration XML
:Most configuration that can be done for the autopilot software is editable through an XML file located in the root of the autopilot repository. When the autopilot is compiled with 'make' this config file is copied to the build directory, and when the autopilot is run it uses the config.xml file found in the current working directory (wherever the autopilot was run from).

;Logging System
:Logging is done by creating an instance of the Logger class, and specifying a prefix and a log level: 
*Prefix: a string which will be prepended to any log messages for that Logger
*Log Level: any message that is sent to the Logger instance that is lower than the specified level will not be logged

;~MavLink Messages [ [[more info|Mavlink Messages]] ]
:This is the message protocol used to communicate with QGroundControl. The message sending and receiving are handled by the QGCLink, QGCSend, and QGCReceive classes. QGCSend polls all active drivers using their sendMavlinkMsg() method to fill its message queue. Drivers pack their own MAVLink messages in their sendMavlinkMsg() method using the mavlink_msg_pack() functions available through the headers in the UDenverMavlink repository.

* Common (default) messages currently in use:
** RC Channels Raw
** RC Channels Scaled
** Control Effort
** Param Value (generic additional parameter)
** Sys Status
** System Time
** Global Position Int (GPS position as integer)
** Radio Calibration
** Scaled IMU
** Heartbeat
** Status Text
* Custom UAlberta/UDenver messages currently in use:
** UAlberta Control Effort
** UAlberta Position
** UAlberta Attitude
** UAlberta GX3 Message
** UAlberta Altimeter
** UAlberta Sys Status
** UAlberta Action
** UDenver CPU Usage
** Novatel GPS Raw

;Web Interface
:A Golang web server is included in the autopilot repository that runs on the autopilot computer, to be accessed via web browser on the ground station machine. It allows for remote control and configuration of the autopilot software.
* Located at: 
```
autopilot/utils/autopilot_web_2.0
```
* Username/Password: otto/otto
* Allows access/downloading of log files
* Upload/manage different autopilot versions
* Upload/modify config.xml files for different autopilot versions
* Start/Stop autopilot software
* Shutdown autopilot computer

;External Libraries
:The following external libraries are included in 'autopilot/src/extern':

* GeographicLib
** Useful GPS position classes
* asio
** Asynchronous IO libraries that allowed us to remove BOOST dependencies
* gtest
** Google's unit testing suite for C++

;Doxygen
:The autopilot software is partially self-documenting via Doxygen. The Doxygen documentation is auto-generated when the project source is compiled with 'make'.
* Can be accessed via web browser at:
```
autopilot/doc/html/index.html
```
* Includes function call graph.

        "$:/language/Help/server": {
            "title": "$:/language/Help/server",
            "description": "Provides an HTTP server interface to TiddlyWiki",
            "text": "The server built in to TiddlyWiki5 is very simple. Although compatible with TiddlyWeb it doesn't support many of the features needed for robust Internet-facing usage.\n\nAt the root, it serves a rendering of a specified tiddler. Away from the root, it serves individual tiddlers encoded in JSON, and supports the basic HTTP operations for `GET`, `PUT` and `DELETE`.\n\n```\n--server <port> <roottiddler> <rendertype> <servetype> <username> <password> <host> <pathprefix>\n```\n\nThe parameters are:\n\n* ''port'' - port number to serve from (defaults to \"8080\")\n* ''roottiddler'' - the tiddler to serve at the root (defaults to \"$:/core/save/all\") \n* ''rendertype'' - the content type to which the root tiddler should be rendered (defaults to \"text/plain\")\n* ''servetype'' - the content type with which the root tiddler should be served (defaults to \"text/html\")\n* ''username'' - the default username for signing edits\n* ''password'' - optional password for basic authentication\n* ''host'' - optional hostname to serve from (defaults to \"127.0.0.1\" aka \"localhost\")\n* ''pathprefix'' - optional prefix for paths\n\nIf the password parameter is specified then the browser will prompt the user for the username and password. Note that the password is transmitted in plain text so this implementation isn't suitable for general use.\n\nFor example:\n\n```\n--server 8080 $:/core/save/all text/plain text/html MyUserName passw0rd\n```\n\nTo run multiple TiddlyWiki servers at the same time you'll need to put each one on a different port.\n"
        },
        "$:/language/Help/setfield": {
            "title": "$:/language/Help/setfield",
            "description": "Prepares external tiddlers for use",
            "text": "//Note that this command is experimental and may change or be replaced during the TiddlyWiki version 5 beta//\n\nSets the specified field of a group of tiddlers to the result of wikifying a template tiddler with the `currentTiddler` variable set to the tiddler.\n\n```\n--setfield <filter> <fieldname> <templatetitle> <rendertype>\n```\n\nThe parameters are:\n\n* ''filter'' - filter identifying the tiddlers to be affected\n* ''fieldname'' - the field to modify (defaults to \"text\")\n* ''templatetitle'' - the tiddler to wikify into the specified field. If blank or missing then the specified field is deleted\n* ''type'' - the text type to render (defaults to \"text/plain\"; \"text/html\" can be used to include HTML tags)\n\n"

            "text": "/*\\\ntitle: $:/core/modules/commander.js\ntype: application/javascript\nmodule-type: global\n\nThe $tw.Commander class is a command interpreter\n\n\\*/\n(function(){\n\n/*jslint node: true, browser: true */\n/*global $tw: false */\n\"use strict\";\n\n/*\nParse a sequence of commands\n\tcommandTokens: an array of command string tokens\n\twiki: reference to the wiki store object\n\tstreams: {output:, error:}, each of which has a write(string) method\n\tcallback: a callback invoked as callback(err) where err is null if there was no error\n*/\nvar Commander = function(commandTokens,callback,wiki,streams) {\n\tvar path = require(\"path\");\n\tthis.commandTokens = commandTokens;\n\tthis.nextToken = 0;\n\tthis.callback = callback;\n\tthis.wiki = wiki;\n\tthis.streams = streams;\n\tthis.outputPath = path.resolve($tw.boot.wikiPath,$tw.config.wikiOutputSubDir);\n};\n\n/*\nAdd a string of tokens to the command queue\n*/\nCommander.prototype.addCommandTokens = function(commandTokens) {\n\tArray.prototype.push.apply(this.commandTokens,commandTokens);\n};\n\n/*\nExecute the sequence of commands and invoke a callback on completion\n*/\nCommander.prototype.execute = function() {\n\tthis.executeNextCommand();\n};\n\n/*\nExecute the next command in the sequence\n*/\nCommander.prototype.executeNextCommand = function() {\n\tvar self = this;\n\t// Invoke the callback if there are no more commands\n\tif(this.nextToken >= this.commandTokens.length) {\n\t\tthis.callback(null);\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Get and check the command token\n\t\tvar commandName = this.commandTokens[this.nextToken++];\n\t\tif(commandName.substr(0,2) !== \"--\") {\n\t\t\tthis.callback(\"Missing command\");\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tcommandName = commandName.substr(2);             "text": "/*\\\ntitle: $:/core/modules/filters.js\ntype: application/javascript\nmodule-type: wikimethod\n\nAdds tiddler filtering methods to the $tw.Wiki object.\n\n\\*/\n(function(){\n\n/*jslint node: true, browser: true */\n/*global $tw: false */\n\"use strict\";\n\n/*\nParses an operation within a filter string\n\tresults: Array of array of operator nodes into which results should be inserted\n\tfilterString: filter string\n\tp: start position within the string\nReturns the new start position, after the parsed operation\n*/\nfunction parseFilterOperation(operators,filterString,p) {\n\tvar operator, operand, bracketPos, curlyBracketPos;\n\t// Skip the starting square bracket\n\tif(filterString.charAt(p++) !== \"[\") {\n\t\tthrow 1);\n\t\t\toperator.operator = operator.operator.substring(0,colon) || \"field\";\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Empty operator means: title\n\t\telse if(operator.operator === \"\") {\n\t\t\toperator.operator = \"title\";\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tp = nextBracketPos + 1;\n\t\tswitch (bracket) {\n\t\tcase '{': // Curly brackets\n\t\t\toperator.indirect = true;\n\t\t\tnextBracketPos = filterString.indexOf('}',p);\n\t\t\tbreak;\n\t\tcase '[': // Square brackets\n\t\t\tnextBracketPos = filterString.indexOf(']',p);\n\t\t\tbreak;\n\t\tcase '/': // regexp brackets\n\t\t\tvar rex = {\n\t\t\toperator.operand = filterString.substring(p,nextBracketPos);\n\t\t}\n\t\tp = nextBracketPos + 1;\n\t\t\t\n\t\t// Push this operator\n\t\toperators.push(operator);\n\t} [[Getting Started]]
Welcome to the University of Denver Helicopter Autopilot Project.

Overview Links:

* [[Autopilot Hardware]]
* [[Autopilot Software]]
* [[Ground Control System]]
* [[MAVLink Messages]]

Currently the code is maintained in 3 separate Git repositories:

* [ext[autopilot|http://www.github.com/josephlewis42/autopilot]]
** This is the [[Autopilot Software]]
* [ext[UDenverQGC|http://www.github.com/josephlewis42/UDenverQGC]]
** A custom version of QGroundControl software
* [ext[UDenverMavlink|http://www.github.com/josephlewis42/UDenverMavlink]]
** Custom and common definitions/headers for [[MAVLink Messages]]

To setup for basic development and use:

* Clone each repository so that the individual folders for all repositories are within the same parent directory. e.g.:
```
project/autopilot/...
project/UDenverQGC/...
project/UDenverMavlink/...
```
* In each repository, consult the README.md file for instructions on compiling and running the individual subsystem
The ground control system consists of the following:

* A Toughbook laptop running Ubuntu Linux
* [[Microhard Radio]]
* [[Novatel GPS]] (this is in addition to the GPS in the [[autopilot box|Autopilot Hardware]]).
* Power Supply (12V)
** -> Novatel GPS
** -> Can power Microhard Radio
** -> Power supply breakout


;Laptop ~WiFi / LAN
:In order to get the [[Microhard Radio]] communication working, its necessary to tell Ubuntu to share the LAN connection ("Wired") with other computers.
* This can be done in Ubuntu via: 
** Network Connections -> 
** Wired connection 1 -> 
** Edit ->
** IPv4 Settings ->
** Method -> Share to other computers

;~QGroundControl (QGC)
:The Toughbook laptop runs a customized version of the ~QGroundControl software in order to track and control the helicopter autopilot. The ground control station and the autopilot box communicate via their own [[Microhard Radios|Microhard Radio]] using standard and custom [[MAVLink Messages]].

;UDenver Plugins
:These are the custom QGC plugins built for interacting with the UDenver autopilot:
* Autopilot Control
** Unified plugin to display statistics and send actions/commands to the autopilot software.
** To modify the UI of this plugin requires QTCreator IDE. The UI file and plugin controller files are located at:
```
UDenverQGC/src/ui/ualberta/UAlbertaControlWidget.*
```
* Remote Autopilot
** This is just a link to the web interface (golang server on autopilot computer)
** This plugin is not necessarily working.
** Files located at:
```
UDenverQGC/src/ui/ualberta/udenverremoteautopilot.*
```

;Adding support for new MAVLink messages
:When new [[MAVLink Messages]] are added to the message definition XML files, and the autopilot is recompiled, the appropriate headers and functions will already be available to QGC. However, QGC needs to be told how to interpret and act upon the new messages once they are received. For receiving messages this can be done by updating the large switch statement in the following file to include the new MAVLink message IDs:
```
UDenverQGC/src/uas/UAlbertaMAV.cc
```

;Radio Calibration
:Some modifications have been made to the RadioCalibration classes in QGC
* More info is needed here...

;How to get plugins in dropdown menu?
:Not sure yet.

no
MAVLink is a standardized messaging protocol for communicating between autopilots and control stations. The MAVLink repository includes many pre-made default (common) messages, as well as the ability to define and add custom messages.

;Usage
:MAVLink message definitions and code are found in the '~UDenverMavlink' repository. Both the 'autopilot' and '~UDenverQGC' repositories reference the '~UDenverMavlink' repo when compiling, which is why the directory structure needs to be maintained (all 3 repos within the same parent). Messages are packed by either QGC or the autopilot software before being sent over the network, and then are unpacked and interpreted when they are received on the other end.

;Modifying/adding messages
:Messages are described in XML files in the 'message_definitions' folder in the '~UDenverMavlink' repository. The common messages may have been slightly altered from the defaults, and any custom messages are defined in the following file:
```
UDenverMavlink/message_definitions/ualberta.xml
```
:Before actually using the messages, the XML files need to be converted to C++ classes by an included generator (written in Python):
```
UDenverMavlink/mavgenerate.py
```
: the C++ classes are also auto-generated when the autopilot is compiled with 'make'.

;Using the new messages
:Once the new messages are implemented and the classes are generated, either QGC or the autopilot software, or both, need to be updated to use and interpret the new messages. What needs to be modified and where will depend on the usage of the new messages but the following are likely to be places that might need updating in order to use the new classes, functions, and message IDs:
* A new Driver's sendMavlinkMsg() method
* autopilot/src/drivers/qgclink/~QGC_Send.cc
* autopilot/src/drivers/qgclink/~QGC_Receive.cc
* ~UDenverQGC/src/uas/~UAlbertaMAV.cc
* QGC class for sending messages?
